All Reviews

  1. I love this set of makeup brushes! It has had, for me, almost everything I've needed as I've grown into using makeup more and getting better at it as well. The only thing I feel is missing from this is a plain paddle-shaped brush, which is usually used for packing on eyeshadow, or patting on glitters. That's harder to do with the crease and blending brush.<br /><br />However, I do highly recommend this set.   333. Base Shadow Brush – Just to clarify since the picture is a little unclear-- this is a round brush. I use this brush on a weekly basis, and it's really nice. I never use it to apply eyeshadow, because it's just too big. I use it mostly as a blending brush for my crease shadow. It's also great for concealer if you have a large spot to cover, as you can use it as a mini stipling brush. Sometimes I use it to apply highligher or small contour (around the nose or chin). It's also great for applying a wash of color anywhere above the lid. Admittedly, I would get more eyeshadow use out of it if it was smaller, but I do like its applications as a face brush. Great for blending.<br /><br />Deluxe Crease Brush – I don't use this as a crease brush. I prefer a round brush with longer bristles for the crease, like the Mac 219, or bdellium 781 (bdellium is a great line of cruelty-free brushes). I use this brush for blending and sometimes applying to the lid.<br /><br />Accent Brush – A nice little brush. Works nicely on brows, eyeliner, or pinpoint applications.<br /><br />Pixel-Point Eyeliner Brush - Out of my entire set of RT brushes, this is the one that gets the least use. The bristles are too long for eyeliner application, too round and flexible for pinpoint concealing. I have no use for this brush. I recommend the bdellium 710 for eyeliner and pinpoint concealing.<br /><br />Brow Brush – I find this brush to be a bit too thick to use on my brows, but that is personal preference. I don't fill in my brows with a brush very much. I use this brush for blending eyeliner or shadow on my lashline.<br /><br />Panoramic 2-in-1 brush case/stand – Meh, I tossed this because I found it a pain to use. I didn't like that it was always open and that my brushes weren't sealed off from the outside environment when the case was closed. I would prefer if they came in a case like the Sigma brushes, or if they included a cute little bag to keep them in, but that's just me. I don't like having to put each brush back into a specific place, and I feel like this gets dirty and isn't easy to clean.<br /><br />I could do my entire face with these three brushes. I would say that this is my favorite set of brushes out of all the RT brush sets.<br /><br />I've had the full set of these brushes since they first launched in 2012. Since getting them, I've used at least three of them every single day. That's two years of constant use, and they look and preform the same way they did the day I received them. Since getting the full line of these, I have not purchased a single new brush. My old mac brushes lay untouched in the back of my drawer. Not to mention that just one Mac brush costs as much as the whole set of these ones. Did I mention that you can now buy these at Walmart?<br /><br />These brushes are superior to animal hair brushes in every way. They are cruelty free. They are extremely easy to clean-- I timed myself, and I can wash twenty brushes in seven minutes. They do not get stained. I purposely didn't clean red OCC Lip Tar off of my lip brush for a month, and the lip tar came off as easily as any other product. (I use Trader Joe's Tea Tree Body Wash or just regular Equate hand soap to clean mine.) They don't hold any funky smells or bacteria after washing, since the bristles aren't porous, unlike animal hair bristles. For the same reason, they dry off very fast. My RT face brush takes about 30 minutes to dry if I leave it damp on a washcloth, and I can dry it almost completely in a few seconds if I rub the brush against a sham. I've cleaned and dried my brushes right before using them to do my makeup regularly. My mac brushes take hours (sometimes days) to dry completely, even if I wipe them against a sham first. Another advantage of the non-porous bristles is that you don't have to condition them. After washing animal hair brushes, you are supposed to condition them with an oil or conditioner so they stay soft and don't get brittle. If you don't, your brushes will start shedding. The RT brushes don't need to be conditioned, and they don't shed.<br /><br />Then, they are soft. Softer than animal hair. They pick up product and dispense it with ease. Product doesn't linger in the brush nearly as much it does on animal hair brushes, which lets me use less product. Truly a pleasure to use and apply makeup with. My one small gripe is that sometimes product can get stuck on the black grip part of these brushes, but that is hardly an issue since it cleans right off. They just might look a bit dirty after rolling around in your makeup bag.<br /><br />These are so durable and have held up better than any brush I've ever had before. As I said before, I've been using them for two years already and they look and feel the same way they did the day I got them. I'm sure that they will last for years to come. I would give these to a friend. I would repurchase. Affordable, durable, just a great product. These would be a great gift to anyone that wears makeup. I would recommend these over any other brush on the market. I feel that this is a truly superior product in every way.t, your brushes will start shedding. The RT brushes don't need to be conditioned, and they don't shed.<br /><br />Then, they are soft. Softer than animal hair. They pick up product and dispense it with ease. The pixel point brush is one that I use very rarely only because I use eye liners with built in applicators, but again, if you needed a precision brush, it would do nicely.   762. I recently decided to start doing my makeup like a grown-up, which meant throwing out the blue eye shadow (or at least hiding it in the back of the cabinet), picking up a nice, nude palette, and finally investing in some makeup brushes instead of those crappy, spongy applicators. Because I don't have a lot of experience doing my makeup nicely, I didn't want to blow a hundred bucks on a set of professional brushes. This set seemed like a good starting point until I understood a bit more about applying makeup and could decide what types of brushes were worth investing in. For the most part I find myself only using the largest 2 brushes. The eyeliner brush is a little to thick and not pointed enough to feasibly use with liquid eyeliner. I don't put makeup on my eyebrows, so the eyebrow brush doesn't get much use either. I occasionally use the accent brush, but it's a little sloppy (the fibers aren't dense enough) to really do a good job. I really love the deluxe crease brush for applying my base colors, although it's way too big to use on your crease. It's nice and stiff so it makes a good blending brush too. The base shadow brush is really the only one in this set that does what it's labeled to do. I will say that for the price I'm not disappointed with this set. The brushes are all soft, and none of the fibers have fallen out. I like that the tips are light colored, so I can actually see how much powder I've picked up. If you're an eye-makeup novice like me and looking for a set to get you started, this isn't a bad way to go. It won't be long, however, before you start replacing the brushes in this set with more expensive, better shaped brushes.

  831. I ABSOLUTELY LOVE these brushes. I'll splurge on eyeshadow palettes all of the time, but I can't stand dropping more than 10 bucks on a single brush. So, when I came across this kit, I was skeptical yet intrigued. It visually stood out to me from other brushes that quite frankly, looked a little cheap. The bristles are dense yet soft, and even though they DO pick up product well, I didn't find the application amount to be satisfactory for me. However, you can use a cheap eyeshadow brush and it's fine. However, it is undebatable that the brushes distribute the shadow perfectly and evenly. Usually when I blend, I find that the bristles will pick up some color and then deposit it elsewhere, so I really have to work the brush to not have a spotty crease color. This is pretty much why I bought the set; watching tutorials online, I noticed that most women use a soft domed brush for blending. Yup! The base shadow brush has become my crease's best friend. The great thing is that there is a variety of brushes; it's not like some kits where you get several that look very similar and are just different sizes. If you are even considering buying brushes, I'd get these. The great thing, especially if you are a &#34;starter&#34;, is that there is a website by the designer with tutorials, so you can learn how to do makeup with the very brushes you own. I wish I had that luxury in the beginning. Also, doing the crease/outer v is typically hard for beginners, and you'll be able to do it like a pro with these brushes. I've gotten good at it on brushes that take me so much longer to do it. This has literally cut my application time in half. I hope you enjoy these, and that this is helpful, especially since I know I'm rambling.
